<span id="freeTextContainer6777113150083719710">Loved this to pieces. From characters and setting, to prose and pace, every single aspect of the book was magnificent. If I could give it 6 stars, I would.<br/>There's no point of reviewing such a popular book though, so I'll simply share some of my thoughts for people who have already read it. Spoilers ahead! <br/><br/><br/><b>PLOT</b><br/>While things seemed complicated at first, I knew that they would come together in the end, so I enjoyed trying to puzzle stuff together and figure out everyone's motives and whatnot. Unfort</span>
  <span id="freeText6777113150083719710" style="display:none">Loved this to pieces. From characters and setting, to prose and pace, every single aspect of the book was magnificent. If I could give it 6 stars, I would.<br />There's no point of reviewing such a popular book though, so I'll simply share some of my thoughts for people who have already read it. Spoilers ahead! <br /><br /><br /><b>PLOT</b><br />While things seemed complicated at first, I knew that they would come together in the end, so I enjoyed trying to puzzle stuff together and figure out everyone's motives and whatnot. Unfortunately though, some things didn't make sense, and most specifically the Empire's plans. <br />We are about to face our biggest enemy atm, the Lord of the Moon's Spawn. Let's just kill our own wizards instead before finishing the enemy! <br />We want to hire the local assassins of a city to murder the city's leaders, so we will naturally assign this job to the only motherfuckers that we don't trust!<br />We will free a Jaghut Tyrant in the hope that our enemy will be forced to face him, but we won't unleash the most powerful demon in our disposal in the same time to call it a success! No! We will send them one after the other to make sure our enemies manage to defeat them! <br /><br /><b>MAGIC SYSTEM</b><br />It doesn't make sense at all. I loved it! Everyone is immensely powerful and scared of everyone else at the same time. It sounds stupid but it isn't - it keeps you on your toes at all times since you don't know what to expect, and who will come on top.<br /><br /><b>CHARACTERS</b><br /><b>-Anomander Rake-</b><br />That's the second baddest motherfucker in the history of bad motherfuckers. He's immortal, he's overpowered as fuck, and he doesn't give a fuck. <br /><br /><b>-Ammanas and Cotillion-</b><br />My favorite characters! Interesting to see how while both of them are Ascendants with immense power they know not to fuck with Rake. I had trouble with the mystery surrounding them though. One on hand, Erikson pretends like their identity is a huge mystery, while who they are is clear to the reader from the very first chapter. On the other hand, their actions didn't make any sense. What did they try to accomplish in the first chapter? Why did Cotillion withdraw from Sorry after managing to infiltrate the Bridgeburners?<br /><br /><b>-Bridgeburners-</b><br />The most interesting characters among them were Kalam and Quick Ben. I love how Quick Ben pretends to be an average wizard for the whole book, and in the end he just casually opens 7 warrens all at once and fucks things up. <br /><br /><b>-Ganoes Paran-</b><br />Disliked him in the beginning, but he kinda grew on me in the end. Dude had the weirdest psychological profile - clearly mental unbalanced, which made for some interesting confrontations with the Gods. <br /><br /><b>-Phoenix Inn regulars-</b><br />My favorite bunch of misfits, except Crokus whom I hated with a passion. Wanted to bitch-slap that little fucker with every turn of the page. Murillio, Rallick, Coll and Kruppe made the best team though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6777113150083719710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer628473580145345536">☣️ <b>And Thus I Signed My Death Warrant</b> <s>DNF</s> Buddy Read (ATISMDWBR™) with some lovely people <s>of slightly despicable book taste</s> over at BB&B ☣️<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>💀 <b>DNF at 75%</b>. <i>No comment and stuff.</i><br/><br/><i><s>Friendly</s> warning: grab a snack and get a drink, this whole lot of nuthin' should take a while.</i><br/><br/>➽ This crappy non-review is dedicated to all those <b>Brave Little Barnacles</b> (BLB™) out there who went the nefarious way and had the audacity to NOT luuurrrrrve this book. Consider my subaquatic kingdom a safe haven from the <b>Erikson Ho</b></span>
  <span id="freeText628473580145345536" style="display:none">☣️ <b>And Thus I Signed My Death Warrant</b> <s>DNF</s> Buddy Read (ATISMDWBR™) with some lovely people <s>of slightly despicable book taste</s> over at BB&amp;B ☣️<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>💀 <b>DNF at 75%</b>. <i>No comment and stuff.</i><br><br><i><s>Friendly</s> warning: grab a snack and get a drink, this whole lot of nuthin' should take a while.</i><br><br>➽ This crappy non-review is dedicated to all those <b>Brave Little Barnacles</b> (BLB™) out there who went the nefarious way and had the audacity to NOT luuurrrrrve this book. Consider my subaquatic kingdom a safe haven from the <b>Erikson Horde of Doom</b> (EHoD™), who shall no doubt persecute you mercilessly for <s>being more clear headed than they are</s> showing such disgusting lack of judgement. <br><br>➘ <b>Disclaimer #1</b>: I had no shrimping idea this series had been inspired by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/54284-the-chronicles-of-the-black-company" rel="nofollow noopener">The Most Wondrous Black Company</a> before I started reading this delightful little book. Had I known about it, I probably would have added Gardens of the <s>Silly</s> Moon to my <b>Bookshelf of Instant Oblivion and Spontaneous Combustion</b> (BoIOaSC™) directly. Because one does not toy around with Glen Cook. Because Glen Cook is Glen Cook. And because <b>Glen Cook is a God</b>. QED and stuff.<br><br>➘ <b>Disclaimer #2</b>: I have a <b>Particularly Scrumptious Scapegoat</b> (PSS™) to blame for the present debacle, my Lovely Decapods. Oh yes. This is all my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Canadian Nemesis'</a> fault, you see. He is the one who <s>forced me to read</s> kindly introduced me to The Lusciously Luscious Black Company, <b>thus ruining me forever</b>. <br><br>➘ <b>Disclaimer #3</b>: I am slightly obsessed by <b>The Most Yummilicious Black Company</b> ← <i>this in case you hadn't noticed. You are most welcome and stuff.</i><br><br>➘ <b>Disclaimer #4</b>: I must have read this book <b>very wrong indeed</b>, because despite its "you make me feel like a total moron" reputation, it didn't confuse me at all. Nope nope nope. <b>Feel like a complete retard</b> while <s>DNFing</s> reading this fantastically thrilling story I did not. Which is highly suspicious. And probably means I'm the biggest of them all. Retard, I mean. <b>Which is impossible</b>. Because we all know I am superiorly intelligent. Which leads me to the following conclusions: I did NOT read this book wrong, should be a member of MENSA and you, <b>Charming Arthropods</b> are, well, how could I put this gently…Not the brightest invertebrates this side of the Seven Seas, shall we say? You're not offended now, are you? <b>Oh, good</b>. <br><br>➘ <b>Disclaimer #5</b>: boo. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489592928ra/22230221.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Why hello there.</i><br><br><b>Sooooo</b>, I was not going to rate this <b>glorious masterpiece of fantasy literature</b> here because I <s>was scared shitless of the EHoD™</s> didn't want Erikson's <s>hysterical</s> lovely fans to feel insulted and stuff. Kindness, compassion and respect personified, that's me. But then I thought: <b>shrimp it all to hell</b>! Everyone hates me anyway! Let's be bold, let's be audacious, <b>let's face death gleefully</b>! Let's rate this <b>most remarkable bookish endeavour</b> two pathetic little stars! <b>And here we are</b>.<br><br><b>Introducing</b>…The Most Glorious Black Company…<b>Decaf, Watered Down Edition</b>! It won't make you cackle with nefarious joviality! It won't make your black, withered heart tingle! It won't make you want to redecorate your living room with <b>severed heads on pikes</b>! Or wear a necklace of chopped off penises in honour of your favourite goddess! <b>It's diet in everything but in length</b>! The dramatis personae list alone is probably longer than the last <s>ten</s> two books you read! Yay! <b>It's beautiful</b>! It's grand! It's bloody shrimping luxurious! And monumental, too! I lurved it so much I want to read it again! <b>More or less</b>.<br><br><b>I wish</b> I could say this book had been written by <b>Glen Cook's evil twin</b>. You know, the same guy who sometimes defiles My God's name by committing books I never read because they never existed because they are slightly sub-par compared to My God's <b>magnificently ambrosial masterpieces</b>? Yeah, that guy. Well it turns out I can't put the blame on that scumbag. Because it appears that Erikson really did write this book here. Which kind of sucks, because he seems to be <b>quite a nice guy</b>. I mean, he does mention Glen Cook and The Delectably Tasty Black Company in the preface of Gardens of the <s>Silly</s> Moon, which means <b>he can't be wholly evil</b>. It doesn't mean the stuff he writes is, you know, scrumptious and stuff, but it means that, even if I don't like the scrumptious stuff he doesn't write, I won't retaliate by <b>slightly unleashing</b> the murderous crustaceans on him. See, it's not ALL bad. As kinda sorta overrated I might find this book to be, Mr Erikson <b>won't suffer the consequences</b>, and die a slow, painful, horrible death via deadly shrimp. And the moral of this wonderfully fascinating paragraph is: ♫ <b>Always look on the bright side of life and all that crap</b> ♫<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489599513i/22230938.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>At this point</b>, you might find your little selves wondering whether there is <s>a valid</s> another reason that justify my <s>misguided under-appreciation</s> minor dislike of this exquisite little book here. Besides its being a pale copy of <b>The Gorgeously Impeccable Black Company</b>, I mean. Yes indeed, there is. There <u>are</u>, actually. "Are what," you ask? Reasons that justifies my <s>misguided under-appreciation</s> minor dislike of this <b>exquisite little book</b> here, you Silly Barnacles *tries to eyeroll herself to death* *fails miserably* *orders Fleet Admiral DaShrimp to take over with his <a href="https://phys.org/news/2013-09-mantis-shrimp-world-eyesbut.html" rel="nofollow noopener">most awesome compound eyes</a>* Here goes:<br><br>① <b>Smells like</b> <s>teen spirit</s> The Dazzlingly Sumptuous Black Company <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>bet you didn't expect that one</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Yeah, yeah, I know, I got it all wrong here. This book is nothing like The Black Company of Utmost Scrumptiouliciousness. <b>Absolutely not</b>. We're dealing with soldiers here, for Shrimp's sake, not with mercenaries! Besides, the soldiers in question are fighting gods, not their slightly evil bosses with otherworldly powers. <b>BIG difference</b>. And it's not like there is a guy who is a super lite version of my <b>Slightly Yummy Boyfriend Croaker</b> (SYBC™) here, either. And his name is certainly not Whiskeyjack. As for somewhat creepy kids à la Daughter of the Night, there are none to be found in Gardens of the <s>Silly</s> Moon. <b>Nope nope nope</b>. Not a single one. Because the one called <s>Silent</s> <s>Sleepy</s> Sorry doesn't count. Oh, and by the way, some ill-intended people might remark that there is a <b>slight similarity</b> between some names in the two series, but I would never do such a thing. Oh no, not me. <b>See</b>? Turns out I wasn't entirely full of crap when I told you this book had NOTHING in common with The Best Fantasy Series That Ever Was And Ever Will Be (TBFSTEWAEWB™), aka <b>The Amazingly Juicy Black Company</b> ← <i>this is case you were having doubts as to what series I might have been referring to. You're welcome.</i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489661752ra/22236544.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Why hello there again.</i><br><br>② This book might not be the <b>cure to insomnia</b>, but it's pretty damn close. Such beautifully unnecessary descriptions! Such delightfully overwhelming, utterly superfluous blah blah blah-ing sessions! Why have your poor characters do things <b>when they can just talk about them instead</b>?! I am so glad Erikson is such a kind, caring, charitable <s>father</s> author. It's so good of him not to exhaust his <s>wretched offspring</s> characters by keeping them busy with all kinds of active stuff all the time. It's much better for them to rest and ponder about the meaning of life. And it's <b>much more relaxing for the reader, too</b>. I so hate it when so much stuff happens in a book that I can't unwind and chill and take it easy while I'm reading. Boredom fests are such delicious, irresistible treats, <b>I just can't get enough of them</b>!<br><br>③ This series is supposed to be a <b>blood and gore fest</b>. Oooh yes, it's terribly bloody. Oh my. And how gory, too. <b>Yuck yuck yuck ew ew ew</b>. This is positively loathsome and vile and repugnant and stuff. I am <b>most completely and utterly disgusted</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>What is this? Blood and Gore 101 for Care Bears or something?</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428863811i/14488172.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>④ <b>Now</b>. Something <b>really bugged the shrimp out of me here</b>. When I embarked upon this most amazing <s>DNF</s> read, I was told repeatedly <b>not to get attached to the characters</b>. Because Erikson is, you know, evil and stuff, and keeps killing his <b>miserable children</b> off and stuff. So "BEWARE DO NOT GET ATTACHED FOR IF YOU DO YOUR POOR LITTLE HEART WILL SUFFER HORRIBLY," my <b>Dear Friends of the Despicable Book Taste</b> (DFotDBT™) said. Right. Two things here:<br><br>1) <b>I do not have a heart</b> so I couldn't care less. Ok, I do have a heart, but it's black and withered, so it doesn’t count.<br>2) <b>What the bloody freaking shrimp</b> is the point of killing your characters <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>yes, this is a REAL spoiler people, don't say I didn't warn you</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[only to have them be <b>reborn/resuscitated/soul-shifted/whatever</b>??!! I guess I could have survived if this had happened just once, but <b>three bloody shrimping times in a row</b>?! First Hairlock, then Paran and finally Tattersail? You have got to be shrimping me. When you kill a character, you KILL a character! As in, you know, <b>KILL DEAD NEVER TO BE BROUGHT BACK TO LIFE</b> and stuff. You don't rip your readers off by playing Return of the Living Dead at your convenience! And what kind of a cop out is that, anyway? <b>This is outrageous</b>! This is not done! <b>This will not do</b>! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421684558i/13403936.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>To my utmost regret</b>, I have to admit there are two things that I <b>actually liked</b> in this book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>oh please, don't faint on me now, we're almost done here</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I kid you not. First, the <b>female characters</b> are quite mouth-watering. So much so that it almost makes me regret I will not be continuing with this delightful series. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>Don't get overexcited here, my Lovely Arthropods, I said ALMOST</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Second, the <b>action scenes</b> are pretty good. Not that they last long or that there are many to be had, but yes, it is true, the <b>five action-filled seconds</b> to be found in the book are not entirely crappy and stuff. <br><br><b>Tada</b>!<br><br>➽ And the moral of this <b>Yeah Yeah Yeah I Once Again Dared Rate a Book I DNFed and Therefore Deserve to Die a Thousand Excruciating Deaths</b> (YYYIOADRaBIDaTDtDaTED™) is: worry not, my Little Clueless Decapods of the Despicable Book Taste, for one day <b>you too shall see the light</b>, and realize you have been worshipping the wrong series all along!<br><br>➽ And the <i>other</i> moral of this <b>YYYIOADRaBIDaTDtDaTED™</b> is: feel like reading <b>The Titillatingly Flavorsome Black Company of Utter Deliciousness</b> yet? No? Calling the Goodreads Police NOW. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489593134i/22230259.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b><u>Rating</u>: no bloody shrimping idea</b>. <i>I guess we'll just have to wait and see what murderous mood I'm in the day I actually write a review for this marvellous little gem.</i><br><br><b>Thou art not dreaming</b>, my Little Barnacles! I did it once again! I DNFed a book worshipped by millions of <s>clueless</s> people across the universe! <b>Go me</b>!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428389872i/14414736.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ Full <b>Don't Blame me I am Most Completely Innocent This Debacle is Absolutely NOT my Fault Crappy Non Review</b> (DBmIaMCITDiANmFCNR™) to come.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1437434782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1437434782" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1437434782?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1437434782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1237964105551014810">A year or so ago someone PM'ed me on Goodreads out of the blue, practically demanding why I haven't read the Malazan series. I was simultaneously pleased and annoyed, the former because somebody seems to think I am some kind of SF/F guru who can be presumed to have read every worthwhile book in these genres, the latter because it's a bit rude init? Still, a backhanded compliment is better than no compliment, or an actual application of somebody’s backhand on my person.<br/> <br/><i>Gardens of the Moon</i> has a </span>
  <span id="freeText1237964105551014810" style="display:none">A year or so ago someone PM'ed me on Goodreads out of the blue, practically demanding why I haven't read the Malazan series. I was simultaneously pleased and annoyed, the former because somebody seems to think I am some kind of SF/F guru who can be presumed to have read every worthwhile book in these genres, the latter because it's a bit rude init? Still, a backhanded compliment is better than no compliment, or an actual application of somebody’s backhand on my person.<br /> <br /><i>Gardens of the Moon</i> has a reputation for being a “tough read”, which is intriguing because fantasy has always seem easily accessible to me. I seldom select books which are generally viewed as challenging, usually I just like to kick back and read (my idea of leisure reading). Still, the Malazan series is often included in lists of all-time great fantasy novels*, and I do like to keep up with the genre Joneses. So two years after languishing in my TBR list <i>Gardens of the Moon</i> arrived at the top of the pile, I think it’s something to do with stars aligning.<br /> <br />This is indeed a tough read, not in the sense that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338798.Ulysses" title="Ulysses by James Joyce" rel="nofollow noopener">Ulysses</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14942.Mrs__Dalloway" title="Mrs. Dalloway by Virginia Woolf" rel="nofollow noopener"> Mrs. Dalloway</a> are tough. Those are post-modern novels with experimental narrative style. While it is quite well written there is nothing particularly experimental about the prose style of <i>Gardens of the Moon</i>. The difficulty lies in how the author, Steven Erikson, throws the reader in at the deep end of his complex world. I could not make heads or tails of the prologue. Who? Why? What? I suspect that if I had simply soldiered on through the next few chapters things would have gradually fallen into place. However, I am somewhat impatient, I wanted to understand the book right from the first page. I already knew there are online sources for this series so I went to Tor.com’s “<a href="http://www.tor.com/series/malazan-reread-of-the-fallen/" rel="nofollow noopener">Malazan Reread of the Fallen</a>”, where they have done chapter by chapter summaries and analyses, which I found to be extremely useful. So I read their summary of the confusing prologue, and then went back to read Chapter 1 of the book, then read their summary of that chapter, the same back-and-forth process again for Chapter 2 and 3. By the time I was reading the fourth chapter the training wheels came off, I no longer felt the need to keep referring to Tor’s summaries any more. <br /> <br /><i>Gardens of the Moon</i> is set on an unnamed world mostly dominated by the expansionist Malazan Empire. The narrative is told from multiple characters’ points of view, some working for the Malazan Empire, some working to defend their homeland against it. Fortunately for me, the novel is not about armies clashing on battlefields, but about individuals doing their duties for their side, be they spies, assassins, mages, alchemists, or thieves. Beside warfare on the mortal level, there is also a concurrent warfare between gods and immortals. It is not clear who are the “good guys” because there are central “POV” characters from both sides of the conflict, and they all have understandable motivations.<br /><br />A lot of modern epic fantasy series tend to be “low fantasy”, which simply means “not much magic", so little of it around that a lot of characters don't even believe it exists. Wizards and dragons seldom show up and when they do the mundane characters are generally flabbergasted. This current trend** seems to have started with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Game of Thrones</a> and followed by the likes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/276660.Joe_Abercrombie" title="Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener"> Joe Abercrombie</a>’s <i>First Law</i> series and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/73149.Scott_Lynch" title="Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener"> Scott Lynch</a>’s <i>Gentleman Bastard Sequence</i>. The world of the Malazan series bucks this particular trend. Magic is everywhere in <i>Gardens of the Moon</i>, most fights involve magic usage, and at least half the characters seem to wield magic of some kind. The way magic functions in this series is quite interesting, magic requires a power source called “warrens” which are both power conduits and hyperspace-like shortcut passages. <br /><br /><i>Gardens of the Moon</i> features a huge cast of characters, so big that Erikson felt obliged to provide a “dramatis personæ” at the beginning of the book. Some detractors of the book say that the characters are flat or not well developed, this surprises me a little because some of the main characters are vivid, complex and believable. However, as there are so many significant characters that some are inevitably less successfully developed than others.<br /><br />Though this book is a little hard to get into once I became familiar with the setting and the characters I find <i>Gardens of the Moon</i> to be quite fast paced without a dull moment. I imagine the next book in the series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55401.Deadhouse_Gates__The_Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___2_" title="Deadhouse Gates (The Malazan Book of the Fallen, #2) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener"> Deadhouse Gates</a> will be much less challenging because I am already familiar with the setting and the author’s style now. I can’t say I feel committed to reading all ten books in the series, but I am looking forward to the next one. <i>Gardens of the Moon</i> is a lot of fun and I am tempted to rate it at five stars but in all good conscience I cannot because it may require more patience, effort and concentration than some readers are willing to allocate. I have to admire Erikson’s moxie though, for writing such an uncompromising first book in a series, I like that he credits the readers with quite a lot of intelligence (probably excessive credit in my case!). It is a gamble which seems to have paid off as the series is one of the most popular of the epic fantasy genre.<br />____________________________<br /><br />* Sample lists:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.buzzfeed.com/awesomer/fantasy-forever#.dpARW1dN7">http://www.buzzfeed.com/awesomer/fant...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bestfantasybooks.com/top25-fantasy-books.php">http://bestfantasybooks.com/top25-fan...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.listchallenges.com/reddits-top-105-fantasy-novelsseries-of-all-time">http://www.listchallenges.com/reddits...</a><br /><br />** I suppose I could be wrong about this trend as I read a lot more science fiction than fantasy and may have gauged the trend incorrectly.<br /><br /><b>Update Sept 2016:</b> Tor's <a href="http://www.tor.com/2016/09/19/a-beginners-guide-to-malazan-characters-gardens-of-the-moon/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Beginner’s Guide to Malazan Characters: Gardens of the Moon</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1237964105551014810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_381068038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381068038" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381068038?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381068038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14210523768306880272">I like this book a lot. The author says he was inspired by Glen Cook's Black Company, and it shows. This is not an easy read. There are a lot of names to keep track of, places, races, etc. The glossary of major players in the beginning helps a lot; my advice for new readers: use it every time you encounter a new name, or forgot who this once mentioned person is. It does not help that as soon as a subplot gets really exciting (fortunately, this happens a lot), the author switches to another, much</span>
  <span id="freeText14210523768306880272" style="display:none">I like this book a lot. The author says he was inspired by Glen Cook's Black Company, and it shows. This is not an easy read. There are a lot of names to keep track of, places, races, etc. The glossary of major players in the beginning helps a lot; my advice for new readers: use it every time you encounter a new name, or forgot who this once mentioned person is. It does not help that as soon as a subplot gets really exciting (fortunately, this happens a lot), the author switches to another, much slower moving subplot. The ending was slightly anticlimactic. <br /><br />Having said this, the book was impossible to put down, and people say this is the weakest book in the series. A lot of events, action sequences, people, backstabbing, were very memorable. <br /><br />The Malazan Empire is conquering last of the Free Cities on a continent. Finally, only two of them is left. One has a good army, strong leadership, a lot of high-ranking wizards, and an ally whose ancient forgotten magic is unrivaled. The second city does not have any army except for city watch, the leadership is corrupted to high heaven, and is torn by internal conflicts. The city with good defences fell first. Most of the action of the book is centered on the aftermath of this battle and intrigues related to upcoming conquest of the second city. <br /><br />The problem is, there are a lot of groups with different interests related to it (I actually lost count of them). Some want this city to still remain independent, some want for Empire to conquer it, some want for peaceful takeover by the Empire, some want to destroy it, yet some want to destroy the whole world starting with (you guessed it) the city. Considering the range of actors - from humble humans to gods (yes, gods play active parts in there), it is extremely complicated affair. <br /><br />For fantasy fans who are not afraid to tackle complicated plots my advice: read this book now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14210523768306880272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10561934118777551743"><b>2nd Read March 2017</b><br/><br/>This is still a bit of a complicated book with a lot of stuff in it and I'm glad I read it with BB&B so that we could discuss some of the things I wasn't quite picking up on. <br/><br/><b>Problem #1 again</b> is I don't think this is a good book to try and listen too. So much is going on and there are so many PoV shifts that it doesn't matter that the narrator is really pretty good it just makes the entire thing very hard to follow. So since I'm continuing on with this series I will probably h</span>
  <span id="freeText10561934118777551743" style="display:none"><b>2nd Read March 2017</b><br /><br />This is still a bit of a complicated book with a lot of stuff in it and I'm glad I read it with BB&amp;B so that we could discuss some of the things I wasn't quite picking up on. <br /><br /><b>Problem #1 again</b> is I don't think this is a good book to try and listen too. So much is going on and there are so many PoV shifts that it doesn't matter that the narrator is really pretty good it just makes the entire thing very hard to follow. So since I'm continuing on with this series I will probably have to physically read it instead of listen.<br /><br /><b>Problem #2</b> is again the same as before on my first read. There are a lot of characters and PoV shifts and sometimes that makes it hard to keep track of. There is a pretty big world here with the history, cultures, gods, dragons, magics and much much more that it requires a lot of concentration. No a bad thing and I'm hoping as the series goes on it becomes more comfortable but as is it is a little bit of a hot mess at times.<br /><br />I did like this a little more the second time through. Things made slightly more sense and there are characters that I really like from different sides of the conflicts. So I'm not really sure that I'm rooting for a side but I am rooting for some of the characters.<br /><br />This will be my big epic fantasy read for 2017 so one book a month of this intricate series should be doable.<br /><br /><b>Original Review Nov 2014</b><br /><br />This was the hardest I had to work at a book in a long time. There are so many characters, magics, peoples, gods and shear volume of information that I had difficulty keeping track. This diminished my enjoyment a little bit. Also the author doesn't ever definitively give you an answer to situations. There is enough information to draw a conclusion but I still don't have any ideas if the conclusions I've drawn are correct. I don't mind working a little for a good story but I wish I had read a few reviews and knew that going in.<br /><br /><b>Regrets:</b><br />That I tried to listen to this on audio. There is so much information that I really needed to jump back and forth to the glossary to figure out who was talking and saying what. Also the chapter format jumps to multiple PoV in each chapter and it was difficult to follow along with on Audio.<br /><br />I didn't even begin to really like the story until about 50% in. There number of characters made it really difficult to become attached to anyone and I still wasn't sure who or even if there was a side to root for. <br /><br /><b>Hopes:</b><br />This is a completed series and it seems after reading a few reviews that on the second read everything makes much more sense and things from this book flow through the rest of the books. So I hope that knowing I will need to approach my reading a little differently I will enjoy future books a little more with less confusion.<br /><br /><b>Suggestions:</b><br />Tor re-read of the Malazan Book of the Fallen. Good chapter summaries with a lot of the finer points being discussed in the comments section. You might find that a good supplement to your reading.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.tor.com/blogs/2010/04/malazan-re-read-of-the-fallen">http://www.tor.com/blogs/2010/04/mala...</a><br /> <br /><i>Thank you Damian, if/when I continue this series I will definitely look into it as this should make reading better</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7514315048358698634">Malazan is an astonishingly great book.* Tremendous. Many of my friends love Malazan, giving this first book in the series an average 3.81 rating (way to bring it down, Sarah Anne and Becky!), and I love it too. It was great.   <span id="freeText7514315048358698634" style="display:none">Malazan is an astonishingly great book.* Tremendous. Many of my friends love Malazan, giving this first book in the series an average 3.81 rating (way to bring it down, Sarah Anne and Becky!), and I love it too. It was great. Hugely great. <br /><br />Erikson takes the time to build the sense of each character, the workings of their daily life and the way they continued to develop over the course of the book was exquisitely detailed. The plot quickly ramps into action, with events building to a frantic pace that culminated in a moving climax. Each word carefully chosen, no detail irrelevant. The humor threaded through this book had me smiling and giggling as I read on the couch. This is one of those books you can devour in a couple of hours, it's so much fun.<br /><br /><br /><br />*This was a Totally Not Honest review, courtesy of a loaner copy by our friends at the South Central Library System.<br /><br />Initial review:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />let's be honest:<br /><br />never, never, ever again. Too many good books, too little time for a series this demanding, and I don't mean in a brain-stretching, feel-good kind of way. I mean in one of those professional, two-day work-seminars that is supposed to bring you 'personal growth' kind of way. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_28987591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28987591" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1385106-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217535570p2/1385106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28987591?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/1385106-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28987591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7369259077080420420">Gardens of the Moon is the first in Steven Erikson's gargantuan and oddly named fantasy series, Malazan Book of the Fallen. What's odd about it is that it took me THREE tries to get through this first volume. The first two times I tried, I got one or two hundred pages in and just lost interest, mainly because I was confused and didn't know what was going on. But the third time I tried it just clicked and I enjoyed it. Figuring out why this is the case took some thought, and I believe it boils do</span>
  <span id="freeText7369259077080420420" style="display:none">Gardens of the Moon is the first in Steven Erikson's gargantuan and oddly named fantasy series, Malazan Book of the Fallen. What's odd about it is that it took me THREE tries to get through this first volume. The first two times I tried, I got one or two hundred pages in and just lost interest, mainly because I was confused and didn't know what was going on. But the third time I tried it just clicked and I enjoyed it. Figuring out why this is the case took some thought, and I believe it boils down to two basic and interconnected reasons.<br /><br />First, Erikson has an extreme "show, don't tell" kind of style. The very first chapter dumps you head over heels into the middle of an epic storyline full of action, with hardly any exposition at all. There's no narrator saying "Okay, there's this nation called the Malazan Empire, and they've been engaging in a protracted military campaign against a group of allied Free Cities. We're going to enter the story as the Malazan forces prepare to attack one of these cities, which has formed an alliance with this one badass dude who controls a flying fortress. Now, let's talk about the structure of the Malazan military..."<br /><br />No, none of that. Instead, after a brief prologue where you eavesdrop on a few characters, you get action action action and you're left to yourself to figure it all out by paying close attention and making your own inferences based on what's said and done. This is mainly what put me way off balance on my first two attempts at reading this tome.<br /><br />The offsetting effects of show-don't-tell style are exacerbated by something else Erikson does: he eschews many of the typical fantasy staples that usually act as guideposts to new readers. There's a reason why not many books stray from the formula of a hapless youngster being apprenticed to an elder wizard or military veteran or adventurer or whatever who guides him through the world that has been opened up to both him and the reader. It allows the author to slyly provide exposition about the world by having the master explain things to the apprentice while the reader just sort of listens in. And going along with all that, other fantasy staples act as familiar sign posts and landmarks so that you don't get lost.<br /><br />Not so much with Erikson. Sure, his books have wizards and dragons and dudes on horseback slinging swords around, but in general Erikson's world is different enough that you don't necessarily know what's going on, and his staunch adherence to the show-don't-tell method means you gotta figure things out on your own. What's a "warren" and what does it mean when a wizard "enters" one to perform his hocus pocus? That's not explained. Figure it out. Or don't. It's all on you, hapless reader.<br /><br />But eventually I did figure enough of it out, and in time I began to see both Erikson's style and his kicking of conventions to the curb as good things. I enjoyed the story and the richness of the world that he was building. If I've got one complaint it's that at least in this book Erikson can't seem to help upping the ante with how powerful each character or threat gets. Okay, here's these really frightening and legendarily powerful Hound things and --oh, okay, this even tougher dude with a big black sword just killed three of them. Guess they weren't that tough. But this wizard is really powerful oh, no he just got stabbed in the neck by an assassin chick who's apparently even further to the right on the badassedness curve. Now here's a demon king fighting a dragon while a pissed off demigod is kicking over mountains like they were sandcastles RRRAAAWWWWOOOOEERRAAHH PEW! PEW! PEW!<br /><br />After a point it borders on ridiculous, but fortunately there are a number of more mundane (and more interesting) characters to tether things down a bit. I look forward to seeing where he goes with it all in the subsequent books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7369259077080420420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IuLbzJB/K28/6BhJ+x/uzbXdi1/Z6Ncm+dCbXDcKwPoYxLIeKyHiB5jDrCgM6uQSY4JslxdlWUGirt3t+kkyYA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
